Retrieved <span class="nowrap">25 November</span> 2012</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Informe+sobre+l%27estat+de+la+pobresa+i+la+desigualtat+al+Principal+d%27Andorra+%282003%29&amp;rft.pub=Estadistica.ad&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.estadistica.ad%2Fserveiestudis%2Fpublicacions%2FPublicacions%2FPobresa.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAndorra" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></li><li value="5">Before 1999, the <a href="/wiki/French_franc" title="French franc">French franc</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_peseta" title="Spanish peseta">Spanish peseta</a>; the coins and notes of both currencies, however, remained legal tender until 2002. Small amounts of <a href="/wiki/Andorran_diner" title="Andorran diner">Andorran diners</a> (divided into 100 centim) were minted after 1982.</li><li value="6">Also <a href="/wiki/.cat" title=".cat">.cat</a>, shared with <a href="/wiki/Pa%C3%AFsos_Catalans" class="mw-redirect" title="Pa\xc3\xafsos Catalans">Catalan-speaking territories</a>.</li>\n</ol></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Andorra</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xc3\xa6/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">\xc3\xa6</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/\xc9\x94\xcb\x90r/: &#39;ar&#39; in &#39;war&#39;">\xc9\x94\xcb\x90r</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">\xc9\x99</span></span>, <wbr />-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/\xc9\x92r/: &#39;or&#39; in &#39;moral&#39;">\xc9\x92r</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">\xc9\x99</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Andorra.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3e/En-us-Andorra.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Andorra.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span>; <small>Catalan:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Catalan" title="Help:IPA/Catalan">[\xc9\x99n\xcb\x88dor\xc9\x99]</a></span>), officially the <b>Principality of Andorra</b> (<a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>: <i lang="ca">Principat d\'Andorra</i>), also called the <b>Principality of the Valleys of Andorra</b><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> (Catalan: <i lang="ca">Principat de les Valls d\'Andorra</i>), is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereign</a> landlocked <a href="/wiki/Microstate" title="Microstate">microstate</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a>, in the eastern <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a>, bordered by <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> in the north and <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> in the south. Believed to have been created by <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>, Andorra was ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Urgell" class="mw-redirect" title="Count of Urgell">Count of Urgell</a> until 988 when it was transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Urgell" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Urgell">Diocese of Urgell</a>, and the present principality was formed by <a href="/wiki/Par%C3%A9age_of_Andorra_1278" title="Par\xc3\xa9age of Andorra 1278">a charter in 1278</a>. It is known as a <a href="/wiki/Principality" title="Principality">principality</a> as it is a <a href="/wiki/Diarchy" title="Diarchy">diarchy</a> headed by two <a href="/wiki/Co-Princes_of_Andorra" title="Co-Princes of Andorra">Co-Princes</a>: the Catholic <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Urgell" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop of Urgell">Bishop of Urgell</a> in Spain and the <a href="/wiki/President_of_France" title="President of France">President of the Republic of France</a>.\n</p><p>Andorra is the <a href="/wiki/European_microstates" title="European microstates">sixth-smallest nation in Europe</a>, having an area of 468 square kilometres (181&#160;sq&#160;mi)  and a population of approximately 77,281.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Andorran_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Andorran people">Andorrans</a> are a <a href="/wiki/Italic_peoples" title="Italic peoples">Romance</a> ethnic group of originally <a href="/wiki/Catalans" title="Catalans">Catalan</a> descent.<sup id="cite_ref-Minahan_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minahan-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Andorra is the 16th-smallest country in the world by land and 11th-smallest country by population.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Its capital <a href="/wiki/Andorra_la_Vella" title="Andorra la Vella">Andorra la Vella</a> is the highest capital city in Europe, at an elevation of 1,023 metres (3,356 feet) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The official language is <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>, although Spanish, Portuguese, and French are also commonly spoken.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Andorra" title="Tourism in Andorra">Andorra\'s tourism</a> services an estimated 10.2 million visitors annually.<sup id="cite_ref-es2_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-es2-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> It is not a member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, but the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a> is its official currency. It has been a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> since 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, the people of Andorra had <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_life_expectancy" title="List of countries by life expectancy">the highest life expectancy in the world</a> at 81 years, according to the <a href="/wiki/Global_Burden_of_Disease_Study" title="Global Burden of Disease Study">Global Burden of Disease Study</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div cities</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Schools"><span class="tocnumber">10.1</span> <span class="toctext">Schools</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#University_of_Andorra"><span class="tocnumber">10.2</span> <span class="toctext">University of Andorra</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-31"><a href="#Virtual_Studies_Centre"><span class="tocnumber">10.2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Virtual Studies Centre</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#Healthcare"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Healthcare</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#Transport"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Transport</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#Media_and_telecommunications"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Media and telecommunications</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#Sports"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">Sports</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-37"><a href="#Major_achievements"><span class="tocnumber">15.1</span> <span class="toctext">Major achievements</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">17</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">18</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The origin of the word <i>Andorra</i> is unknown, although several hypotheses have been formulated. The oldest derivation of the word <i>Andorra</i> is from the Greek historian <a href="/wiki/Polybius" title="Polybius">Polybius</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Histories_(Polybius)" title="The Histories (Polybius)">The Histories</a></i> III, 35, 1) who describes the <i>Andosins</i>, an <a href="/wiki/Iberians" title="Iberians">Iberian</a> <a href="/wiki/Pre-Roman_peoples_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Pre-Roman peoples of the Iberian Peninsula">Pre-Roman tribe</a>, as historically located in the valleys of Andorra and facing the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Carthage" title="Ancient Carthage">Carthaginian</a> army in its passage through the Pyrenees during the <a href="/wiki/Punic_Wars" title="Punic Wars">Punic Wars</a>. The word <i>Andosini</i> or <i>Andosins</i> (\xe1\xbc\x88\xce\xbd\xce\xb4\xce\xbf\xcf\x83\xce\xaf\xce\xbd\xce\xbf\xce\xb9) may derive from the <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a> <i>handia</i> whose meaning is "big" or "giant".<sup id="cite_ref-Diccionari_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Diccionari-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The Andorran <a href="/wiki/Toponymy" title="Toponymy">toponymy</a> shows evidence of <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque language</a> in the area. Another theory suggests that the word <i>Andorra</i> may derive from the old word <i>Anorra</i> that contains the Basque word <i>ur</i> (water).<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Another theory suggests that <i>Andorra</i> may derive from <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a> <i>al-durra</i>, meaning "The forest" (\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xaf\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa9). When the <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moors</a> colonized the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a>, the valleys of the Pyrenees were covered by large tracts of forest, and other regions and towns, also administered by Muslims, received this designation.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other theories suggest that the term derives from the <a href="/wiki/Navarro-Aragonese" title="Navarro-Aragonese">Navarro-Aragonese</a> <i>andurrial</i>, which means "land covered with bushes" or "scrubland".<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Folk_etymology" title="Folk etymology">folk etymology</a> holds that <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a> had named the region as a reference to the <a href="/wiki/Biblical" class="mw-redirect" title="Biblical">Biblical</a> <a href="/wiki/Cannan" title="Cannan">Canaanite</a> valley of <i><a href="/wiki/Endor_(village)" title="Endor (village)">Endor</a></i> or <i><a href="/wiki/Endor_(village)" title="Endor (village)">Andor</a></i> (where the <a href="/wiki/Midianites" class="mw-redirect" title="Midianites">Midianites</a> had been defeated), a name also bestowed by his heir and son <a href="/wiki/Louis_le_Debonnaire" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis le Debonnaire">Louis le Debonnaire</a> after defeating the Moors in the "wild valleys of Hell".<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Andorra" title="History of Andorra">History of Andorra</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG/220px-Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG/330px-Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG/440px-Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Roc de les Bruixes</i> prehistorical sanctuary located in <a href="/wiki/Canillo" title="Canillo">Canillo</a> (detail)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ann%C3%ADbal,_andosins.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Ann%C3%ADbal%2C_andosins.png/220px-Ann%C3%ADbal%2C_andosins.png" width="220" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Ann%C3%ADbal%2C_andosins.png/330px-Ann%C3%ADbal%2C_andosins.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Ann%C3%ADbal%2C_andosins.png/440px-Ann%C3%ADbal%2C_andosins.png 2x" data-file-width="819" data-file-height="834" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ann%C3%ADbal,_andosins.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hannibal" title="Hannibal">Hannibal</a>\'s route (in red) during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Punic_War" title="Second Punic War">Second Punic War</a>. The Iberian tribes (in green) fought against the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Carthage" title="Ancient Carthage">Carthaginian</a> army in the Pyrenees.</div></div></div>\n<p><i>La Balma de la <a href="/wiki/La_Margineda" title="La Margineda">Margineda</a></i>, found by <a href="/wiki/Archaeologist" class="mw-redirect" title="Archaeologist">archaeologists</a> at <a href="/wiki/Sant_Julia_de_Loria" class="mw-redirect" title="Sant Julia de Loria">Sant Julia de Loria</a>, was first settled in 9,500 BC as a passing place between the two sides of the Pyrenees. The seasonal camp was perfectly located for hunting and fishing by the groups of hunter-gatherers from <a href="/wiki/Ari%C3%A8ge_(river)" title="Ari\xc3\xa8ge (river)">Ariege</a> and <a href="/wiki/Segre_(river)" title="Segre (river)">Segre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Age" class="mw-redirect" title="Neolithic Age">Neolithic Age</a> a group of people moved to the <a href="/wiki/Madriu-Perafita-Claror_Valley" title="Madriu-Perafita-Claror Valley">Valley of Madriu</a> (nowadays Natural Parc located in <a href="/wiki/Escaldes-Engordany" title="Escaldes-Engordany">Escaldes-Engordany</a> declared <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>) as a permanent camp in 6640 BC. The population of the valley grew cereals, raised domestic livestock and developed a commercial trade with people from the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A8gre_(department)" title="S\xc3\xa8gre (department)">Segre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Occitania" title="Occitania">Occitania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200932,_33_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200932,_33-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other archaeological deposits include the <i>Tombs of <a href="/wiki/Segudet" title="Segudet">Segudet</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Ordino" title="Ordino">Ordino</a>) and <i>Feixa del Moro</i> (Sant Julia de Loria) both dated in 490\xe2\x80\x934300 BC as an example of the <a href="/wiki/Urnfield_culture" title="Urnfield culture">Urn culture</a> in Andorra.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200932,_33_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200932,_33-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\nThe model of small settlements begin to evolved as a complex urbanism during the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a>. <a href="/wiki/Metallurgy" title="Metallurgy">Metallurgical</a> items of iron, ancient coins and relicaries can be found in the <a href="/wiki/Sanctuary" title="Sanctuary">ancient sanctuaries</a> scattered around the country.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Sanctuary" title="Sanctuary">sanctuary</a> of <i>Roc de les Bruixes</i> (Stone of the Witches) is maybe the most important archeological complex of this age in Andorra, located in the parish of <a href="/wiki/Canillo" title="Canillo">Canillo</a>, about the rituals of funerals, ancient scripture and engraved stone <a href="/wiki/Mural" title="Mural">murals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200934,_35,_38,_39_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200934,_35,_38,_39-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Iberian_and_Roman_Andorra">The Iberian and Roman Andorra</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: The Iberian and Roman Andorra">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The inhabitants of the valleys were traditionally associated with the <a href="/wiki/Iberians" title="Iberians">Iberians</a> and historically located in Andorra as the Iberian tribe <i>Andosins</i> or <i>Andosini</i> (\xe1\xbc\x88\xce\xbd\xce\xb4\xce\xbf\xcf\x83\xce\xaf\xce\xbd\xce\xbf\xcf\x85\xcf\x82) during the 7th and 2nd centuries BC. Influenced by <a href="/wiki/Aquitanian_language" title="Aquitanian language">Aquitanias</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iberian_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Iberian languages">Iberian languages</a> the locals developed some current toponyms. Early writings and documents relating this group of people goes back to the second century BC by the Greek writer <a href="/wiki/Polybius" title="Polybius">Polybius</a> in his <i>Histories</i> during the <a href="/wiki/Punic_Wars" title="Punic Wars">Punic Wars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200943_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200943-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92_20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200937,_36_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200937,_36-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Some of the most significant remains of this era are the Castle of the <i>Roc d\'Enclar</i> (part of the early <a href="/wiki/Marca_Hispanica" title="Marca Hispanica">Marca Hispanica</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200944,_45,_46,_47_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200944,_45,_46,_47-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> <i>l\'Anxiu</i> in <a href="/wiki/Les_Escaldes" title="Les Escaldes">Les Escaldes</a> and <i>Roc de L\'Oral</i> in <a href="/wiki/Encamp" title="Encamp">Encamp</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92_20-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200937,_36_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200937,_36-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\nThe presence of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a> influence is recorded from the 2nd century BC to the 5th century AD. The places found with more Roman presence are in <i>Camp Vermell</i> (Red Field) in Sant Julia de Loria and in some places in Encamp as well as in the <i>Roc d\'Enclar</i>. People continued trading, mainly with wine and cereals, with the Roman cities of <a href="/wiki/Urgellet" title="Urgellet">Urgellet</a> (nowaday <a href="/wiki/La_Seu_d%27Urgell" title="La Seu d&#39;Urgell">La Seu d\'Urgell</a>) and all across Segre through the <i><a href="/wiki/Roman_roads" title="Roman roads">Via Romana</a> Strata Ceretana</i> (also known as <i>Strata Confluetana</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200952,_53_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200952,_53-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92_20-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200944,_45,_46,_47_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200944,_45,_46,_47-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92_20-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Visigoths_and_Carolingians:_the_legend_of_Charlemagne">The Visigoths and Carolingians: the legend of Charlemagne</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: The Visigoths and Carolingians: the legend of Charlemagne">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg/220px-Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg" width="220" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg/330px-Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg/440px-Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg 2x" data-file-width="447" data-file-height="414" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a> instructing his son <a href="/wiki/Louis_the_Pious" title="Louis the Pious">Louis the Pious</a></div></div></div>\n<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Roman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Fall of the Roman Empire">fall of the Roman Empire</a> Andorra came under the influence of the <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">Visigoths</a>, not remotely from the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Toledo,_Spain#Visigothic_Toledo" title="History of Toledo, Spain">Kingdom of Toledo</a>, but locally from the <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Urgell" class="mw-redirect" title="Diocese of Urgell">Diocese of Urgell</a>. The Visigoths remained in the valleys for 200 years, during which time <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Christianity" title="Gothic Christianity">Christianity</a> spread. When the <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Muslim Empire</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_conquest_of_Hispania" title="Umayyad conquest of Hispania">conquest</a> of the Iberian Peninsula replaced the ruling Visigoths, Andorra was sheltered from these invaders by the <a href="/wiki/Francia" title="Francia">Franks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tradition holds that <i>Charles the Great</i> (<a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>) granted a charter to the Andorran people for a contingent of five thousand soldiers under the command of <i>Marc Almugaver</i>, in return for fighting against the <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moors</a> near <a href="/wiki/Port%C3%A9-Puymorens" title="Port\xc3\xa9-Puymorens">Port\xc3\xa9-Puymorens</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cerdanya" title="Cerdanya">Cerdanya</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png/220px-Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png/330px-Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png/440px-Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png 2x" data-file-width="591" data-file-height="400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The six old parishes named by their <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saint</a> as depicted in the <i>Acta de Consagraci\xc3\xb3 i Dotaci\xc3\xb3 de la Catedral de la Seu d\'Urgell</i> (839)</div></div></div>\n<p>Andorra remained part of the Marca Hispanica of the <a href="/wiki/Frankish_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankish Empire">Frankish Empire</a> being part of the territory ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Urgell" class="mw-redirect" title="Count of Urgell">Count of Urgell</a> and eventually by the <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Urgel" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop of Urgel">bishop</a> of the Diocese of Urgell. Also tradition holds that it was guaranteed by the son of Charlemagne, <a href="/wiki/Louis_the_Pious" title="Louis the Pious">Louis the Pious</a>, writing the <i>Carta de Poblament</i> or a local <a href="/wiki/Municipal_charter" title="Municipal charter">municipal charter</a> circa 805.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 988, <a href="/wiki/Borrell_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Borrell II">Borrell II</a>, Count of Urgell, gave the Andorran valleys to the Diocese of Urgell in exchange for land in Cerdanya.<sup id="cite_ref-histo1_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-histo1-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Since then the Bishop of Urgell, based in Seu d\'Urgell, has been <a href="/wiki/Co-Princes_of_Andorra" title="Co-Princes of Andorra">Co-prince</a> of Andorra.<sup id="cite_ref-elements_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elements-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first document that mentions <i>Andorra</i> as a territory is the <i>Acta de Consagraci\xc3\xb3 i Dotaci\xc3\xb3 de la Catedral de la Seu d\'Urgell</i> (Deed of Consecration and Endowment of the Cathedral of La Seu d\'Urgell). The old document dated from 839 depicts the six old <a href="/wiki/Parishes_of_Andorra" title="Parishes of Andorra">parishes</a> of the Andorran valleys and therefore the administrative division of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Medieval_Age:_The_Par.C3.A9ages_and_the_founding_of_the_Co-Principality"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_Age:_The_Par\xc3\xa9ages_and_the_founding_of_the_Co-Principality">Medieval Age: The Par\xc3\xa9ages and the founding of the Co-Principality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Medieval Age: The Par\xc3\xa9ages and the founding of the Co-Principality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg/220px-Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg/330px-Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg/440px-Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2922" data-file-height="1864" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sant_Joan_de_Caselles" title="Sant Joan de Caselles">Sant Joan de Caselles</a> church, dating from the 11th century, part of the Andorran Romanesque heritage</div></div></div>\n<p>Before 1095, Andorra did not have any type of military protection and the Bishop of Urgell, who knew that the Count of Urgell wanted to reclaim the Andorran valleys,<sup id="cite_ref-elements_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elements-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> asked the <a href="/wiki/Lord_of_Caboet" title="Lord of Caboet">Lord of Caboet</a> for help and protection. In 1095 the Lord of Caboet and the Bishop of Urgell signed under oath a declaration of their co-sovereignty over Andorra. Arnalda, daughter of Arnau of Caboet, married the Viscount of Castellb\xc3\xb2 and both became Viscounts of Castellb\xc3\xb2 and Cerdanya. Years later their daughter, Ermessenda,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> married <a href="/wiki/Roger-Bernard_II,_Count_of_Foix" title="Roger-Bernard II, Count of Foix">Roger Bernat II</a>, the French <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Foix" title="Count of Foix">Count of Foix</a>. They became Roger Bernat II and Ermessenda I, Counts of Foix, Viscounts of Castellb\xc3\xb2 and Cerdanya, and co-sovereigns of Andorra (shared with the Bishop of Urgell).\n</p><p>In the 13th century, a military dispute arose between the Bishop of Urgell and the Count of Foix as aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Cathar_Crusade" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathar Crusade">Cathar Crusade</a>. The conflict was resolved in 1278 with the mediation of the king of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aragon" title="Kingdom of Aragon">Aragon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pere_el_Gran" class="mw-redirect" title="Pere el Gran">Pere II</a> between the Bishop and the Count,  by the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Par%C3%A9age_of_Andorra_1278" title="Par\xc3\xa9age of Andorra 1278">first par\xc3\xa9age</a> which provided that Andorra\'s sovereignty be shared between the count of Foix<sup id="cite_ref-elements_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elements-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> (whose title would ultimately transfer to the French head of state) and the Bishop of Urgell, in <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a>. This gave the <a href="/wiki/Principality" title="Principality">principality</a> its territory and political form.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJordi_Planellas2013_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJordi_Planellas2013-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg/220px-Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg/330px-Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg/440px-Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1092" data-file-height="714" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Monument commemorating in 1978 the 700th anniversary of the Par\xc3\xa9ages, located outside <a href="/wiki/Casa_de_la_Vall" title="Casa de la Vall">Casa de la Vall</a> in the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Andorra_la_Vella" title="Andorra la Vella">Andorra la Vella</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg/220px-065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg/330px-065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg/440px-065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Apse fresco of <a href="/wiki/Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters" title="Esgl\xc3\xa9sia de Sant Miquel d&#39;Engolasters">Sant Miquel d\'Engolasters</a> church, painted by <i>Mestre de Santa Coloma</i> during the 12th century<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>A second par\xc3\xa9age was signed in 1288 after a dispute when the <a href="/wiki/Roger-Bernard_III,_Count_of_Foix" title="Roger-Bernard III, Count of Foix">Count of Foix</a> ordered the construction of a castle in <i>Roc d\'Enclar</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJordi_Planellas2013_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJordi_Planellas2013-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The document was ratified by the noble notary <a href="/wiki/County_of_Cerdanya" title="County of Cerdanya">Jaume Orig of Puigcerd\xc3\xa0</a> and the construction of military structures in the country was prohibited.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200960,_61_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200960,_61-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146_32-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1364 the political organization of the country named the figure of the <a href="/wiki/Syndic" title="Syndic">syndic</a> (now spokesman and president of the parliament) as representative of the Andorrans to their co-princes making possible the creation of <a href="/wiki/Parishes_of_Andorra" title="Parishes of Andorra">local departments</a> (<i>comuns</i>, <i>quarts</i> and <i>ve\xc3\xafnats</i>). After being ratified by the Bishop Francesc Tovia and the Count <a href="/wiki/John_I,_Count_of_Foix" title="John I, Count of Foix">Jean I</a>, the <i>Consell de la Terra</i> or <a href="/wiki/General_Council_(Andorra)" title="General Council (Andorra)">Consell General de les Valls</a> (General Council of the Valleys) was founded in 1419, the second oldest parliament in Europe. The syndic Andreu d\'Al\xc3\xa0s and the General Council organized the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Andorra#Judicial_branch" title="Politics of Andorra">Justice Courts</a> (<i>La Cort de Justicia</i>) in 1433 with the Co-Princes and the collection of taxes like <i>foc i lloc</i> (literally <i>fire and site</i>, a national tax active since then).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200978,_79,_80,_81,_88,_89_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200978,_79,_80,_81,_88,_89-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Although we can find remains of ecclesiastical works dating before the 9th century (<i>Sant Vicen\xc3\xa7 d\'Enclar</i> or <a href="/wiki/Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Santa_Coloma" class="mw-redirect" title="Esgl\xc3\xa9sia de Santa Coloma">Esgl\xc3\xa9sia de Santa Coloma</a>), Andorra developed exquisite <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_Art_and_Architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanesque Art and Architecture">Romanesque Art</a> during the 9th through 14th centuries, as much in the construction of churches, bridges, religious murals and statues of the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_and_Child" class="mw-redirect" title="Virgin and Child">Virgin and Child</a> (being the most important the <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Meritxell" title="Our Lady of Meritxell">Our Lady of Meritxell</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Nowadays, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_regional_characteristics_of_Romanesque_churches#Romanesque_churches_in_Spain.2C_Portugal_and_Andorra" title="List of regional characteristics of Romanesque churches">Romanesque</a> buildings that form part of <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Heritage_of_Andorra" title="Cultural Heritage of Andorra">Andorra\'s cultural heritage</a> stand out in a remarkable way, with an emphasis on <a href="/wiki/Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Esteve" title="Esgl\xc3\xa9sia de Sant Esteve">Esgl\xc3\xa9sia de Sant Esteve</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sant_Joan_de_Caselles" title="Sant Joan de Caselles">Sant Joan de Caselles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters" title="Esgl\xc3\xa9sia de Sant Miquel d&#39;Engolasters">Esgl\xc3\xa9sia de Sant Miquel d\'Engolasters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sant_Mart%C3%AD_de_la_Cortinada" class="mw-redirect" title="Sant Mart\xc3\xad de la Cortinada">Sant Mart\xc3\xad de la Cortinada</a> and the medieval bridges of <a href="/wiki/Pont_de_la_Margineda" title="Pont de la Margineda">Margineda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pont_dels_Escalls" title="Pont dels Escalls">Escalls</a> among many others.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200948,_49,_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200948,_49,-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGarcia2011_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGarcia2011-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009150_a_194_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009150_a_194-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>While the Catalan Pyrenees were embryonic of the <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan language</a> at the end of the 11th century Andorra was influenced by the appearance of that language where it was adopted by proximity and influence even decades before it was expanded by the rest of the Kingdom of Aragon.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The local population based its economy during the Middle Ages in the livestock and agriculture, as well as in furs and weavers. Later, at the end of the 11th century, the first <a href="/wiki/Bloomery#Medieval_Europe" title="Bloomery">foundries of iron</a> began to appear in Northern Parishes like <a href="/wiki/Ordino" title="Ordino">Ordino</a>, much appreciated by the master artisans who developed the art of the forges, an important economic activity in the country from the 15th century.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnne_Doustaly-Dunyach2011_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnne_Doustaly-Dunyach2011-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="16th_to_18th_centuries">16th to 18th centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 16th to 18th centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tribunal_de_Corts_d%27Andorra.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Tribunal_de_Corts_d%27Andorra.JPG/220px-Tribunal_de_Corts_d%27Andorra.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Tribunal_de_Corts_d%27Andorra.JPG/330px-Tribunal_de_Corts_d%27Andorra.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fc/Tribunal_de_Corts_d%27Andorra.JPG 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="266" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tribunal_de_Corts_d%27Andorra.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Main hall of <a href="/wiki/Andorra#Law_and_criminal_justice" title="Andorra"><i>Tribunal de Corts</i></a> (High Court of Justice) inside <a href="/wiki/Casa_de_la_Vall" title="Casa de la Vall">Casa de la Vall</a>, the central Judiciary Court of Andorra</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1601 the <a href="/wiki/Andorra#Law_and_criminal_justice" title="Andorra">Tribunal de Corts</a> (High Court of Justice) was created as a result of <a href="/wiki/Huguenot_rebellions" title="Huguenot rebellions">Huguenot rebellions</a> from France, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition" title="Spanish Inquisition">Inquisition</a> courts coming from Spain and <a href="/wiki/Catalan_mythology_about_witches" title="Catalan mythology about witches">indigenous witchcraft</a> experienced in the country due to the <a href="/wiki/Reformation" title="Reformation">Reformation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Counter-Reformation" title="Counter-Reformation">Counter-Reformation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199844,_45,_47,_48,_50_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199844,_45,_47,_48,_50-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009108,_109_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009108,_109-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009238,_239_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009238,_239-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009238,_239_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009238,_239-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>  With the passage of time, the co-title to Andorra passed to the kings of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Navarre" title="Kingdom of Navarre">Navarre</a>. After Henry of Navarre became King <a href="/wiki/Henry_IV_of_France" title="Henry IV of France">Henry IV of France</a>, he issued an edict in 1607, that established the head of the French state and the Bishop of Urgell as <a href="/wiki/Co-Princes_of_Andorra" title="Co-Princes of Andorra">Co-Princes of Andorra</a>. During 1617 communal councils form the <i>sometent</i> (popular militia or army) to deal with the rise of <i>bandolerisme</i> (<a href="/wiki/Brigandage" title="Brigandage">brigandage</a>) and the Consell de la Terra was defined and structured in terms of its composition, organization and competences current today .<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199844,_45,_47,_48,_50_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199844,_45,_47,_48,_50-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJordi_Planellas201342_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJordi_Planellas201342-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199853,_54,_56_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199853,_54,_56-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Andorra continued with the same economic system that it had during the 12th-14th centuries with a large production of metallurgy (<i>fargues</i>, a system similar to <i>Farga catalana</i>) and with the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">tobacco</a> circa 1692 and import trade. The <a href="/wiki/Fair" title="Fair">fair</a> of Andorra la Vella was ratified by the co-princes in 1371 and 1448 being the most important annual national festival commercially ever since.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199814_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199814-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199815_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199815-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009134_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009134-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg/220px-Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg/330px-Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg/440px-Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5135" data-file-height="3423" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Manor_house" title="Manor house">Manor house</a> of Rossell family in <a href="/wiki/Ordino" title="Ordino">Ordino</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Casa_Rossell" title="Casa Rossell">Casa Rossell</a></i>, built in 1611. The family owned in 1619 also the largest ironwork forges in Andorra as <i>Farga Rossell</i> and <i>Farga del Serrat</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The country had a unique and experienced <a href="/wiki/Guild" title="Guild">guild</a> of weavers, <i>Confraria de Paraires i Teixidors</i>, located in <a href="/wiki/Escaldes-Engordany" title="Escaldes-Engordany">Escaldes-Engordany</a> founded in 1604 taking advantage of the thermal waters of the area. By that time the country was characterized by the social system of <i>prohoms</i> (wealthy society) and <i>casalers</i> (rest of the population with smaller economic acquisition), deriving from the tradition of <i><a href="/wiki/Pubilla" title="Pubilla">pubilla</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Heir" class="mw-redirect" title="Heir"><i>hereu</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199820,_21_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199820,_21-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni2009106,_107_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni2009106,_107-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009105,_106,_107,_140,_141_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009105,_106,_107,_140,_141-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009263_a_270_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009263_a_270-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Three centuries after its foundation the Consell de la Terra located its headquarters and the Tribunal de Corts in <a href="/wiki/Casa_de_la_Vall" title="Casa de la Vall">Casa de la Vall</a> in 1702. The <a href="/wiki/Manor_house" title="Manor house">manor house</a> built in 1580 served as a noble fortress of the Busquets family. Inside the parliament was placed the <i>Closet of the six keys</i> (<i>Armari de les sis claus</i>) representative of each Andorran parish and where the <a href="/wiki/Andorran_constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="Andorran constitution">Andorran constitution</a> and other documents and laws were kept later on.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199860_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199860-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200982_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200982-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In both <a href="/wiki/Guerra_dels_Segadors" class="mw-redirect" title="Guerra dels Segadors">Guerra dels Segadors</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guerra_de_Sucesi%C3%B3n_Espa%C3%B1ola" class="mw-redirect" title="Guerra de Sucesi\xc3\xb3n Espa\xc3\xb1ola">Guerra de Sucesi\xc3\xb3n Espa\xc3\xb1ola</a> conflicts, the Andorran people (although with the statement neutral country) supported the <a href="/wiki/Catalans" title="Catalans">Catalans</a> who saw their <a href="/wiki/Catalan_constitutions" title="Catalan constitutions">rights</a> reduced in <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Planta_decrees" title="Nueva Planta decrees">1716</a>. The reaction was the promotion of Catalan writings in Andorra, with cultural works such as the <i>Book of Privileges</i> (<i>Llibre de Privilegis de 1674</i>), <i>Manual Digest</i> (1748) by Antoni Fiter i Rossell or the <i>Polit\xc3\xa0 andorr\xc3\xa0</i> (1763) by Antoni Puig.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009229_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009229-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009229_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009229-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009229_59-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009229-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199849_a_52,_i_57,_58_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199849_a_52,_i_57,_58-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century:_the_New_Reform_and_the_Andorran_Question">19th century: the New Reform and the Andorran Question</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 19th century: the New Reform and the Andorran Question">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit.png/220px-Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit.png" width="220" height="281" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit.png/330px-Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/76/Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit.png 2x" data-file-width="361" data-file-height="461" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Portrait of <a href="/wiki/Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit" title="Guillem d&#39;Areny-Plandolit">Guillem d\'Areny-Plandolit</a>, nobleman and politician who promoted the <i>New Reform</i> in 1866.</div></div></div>\n<p>After the French Revolution, in 1809, Napoleon I reestablished the Co-Principate and deleted the French medieval tithe. However, in 1812\xe2\x80\x9313, the <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">First French Empire</a> annexed Catalonia during the <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">Peninsular War</a> (<i>Guerra del franc\xc3\xa9s</i>). They divided it into four <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9partement" class="mw-redirect" title="D\xc3\xa9partement">d\xc3\xa9partements</a>, with Andorra being made part of the district of <a href="/wiki/Puigcerd%C3%A0" title="Puigcerd\xc3\xa0">Puigcerd\xc3\xa0</a> (d\xc3\xa9partement of <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A8gre" class="mw-redirect" title="S\xc3\xa8gre">S\xc3\xa8gre</a>). In 1814 a royal decree reestablished the independence and economy of Andorra.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009172_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009172-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009172_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009172-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009342,_343_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009342,_343-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During this period, Andorra\'s late medieval institutions and rural culture remained largely unchanged. In 1866 the syndic <a href="/wiki/Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit" title="Guillem d&#39;Areny-Plandolit">Guillem d\'Areny-Plandolit</a> led the <i>reformist</i> group in a Council General of 24 members, elected by suffrage limited to heads of families, replaced the aristocratic oligarchy that previously ruled the state.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The New Reform (<i>Nova Reforma</i> or <i>Pla de Reforma</i>) began after being ratified by both Co-Princes and established the basis of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Andorra" title="Constitution of Andorra">constitution</a> and symbols (such as the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Andorra" title="Flag of Andorra">tricolor flag</a>) of Andorra. A new <a href="/wiki/Service_economy" title="Service economy">service economy</a> arose as a demand of the inhabitants of the valleys and began to build infrastructures such as hotels, spa resorts, roads and telegraph lines.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009192,_193_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009192,_193-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009191,_192,_193_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009191,_192,_193-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009345_a_347_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009345_a_347-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESegal\xc3\xa0s201293_a_95_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESegal\xc3\xa0s201293_a_95-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Revoluci%C3%B3_de_1881_d%27Andorra.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Revoluci%C3%B3_de_1881_d%27Andorra.jpg/220px-Revoluci%C3%B3_de_1881_d%27Andorra.jpg" width="220" height="333" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/47/Revoluci%C3%B3_de_1881_d%27Andorra.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="263" data-file-height="398" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Revoluci%C3%B3_de_1881_d%27Andorra.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Illustration of a scene from the streets of <a href="/wiki/Canillo" title="Canillo">Canillo</a> during the <i>Revolution of 1881</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The authorities of the Co-Princes (<i>veguer</i>) banned casinos and betting houses throughout the country by establishing an economic conflict with the demand of the Andorran people. The conflict led to the so-called <i>Revolution of 1881</i> or <i>Troubles of Andorra</i>, when revolutionaries assaulted the house of the syndic during 8 December 1880 and established the <i>Provisional Revolutionary Council</i> led by Joan Pla i Calvo and Pere Bar\xc3\xb3 i Mas, who granted the construction of casinos and spas to foreign companies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009198,_199,_203_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009198,_199,_203-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> During 7 and 9 June 1881, the loyalists of <a href="/wiki/Canillo" title="Canillo">Canillo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Encamp" title="Encamp">Encamp</a> reconquered the parishes of <a href="/wiki/Ordino" title="Ordino">Ordino</a> and <a href="/wiki/Massana" class="mw-redirect" title="Massana">Massana</a> by establishing contact with the revolutionary forces in <a href="/wiki/Escaldes-Engordany" title="Escaldes-Engordany">Escaldes-Engordany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeruga_Guerrero199859,_60,_63_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeruga_Guerrero199859,_60,_63-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>  After a day of combat finally the <a href="/wiki/Pont_dels_Escalls" title="Pont dels Escalls">Treaty of the Bridge of Escalls</a> was signed on 10 June.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMinisteri_d&#39;Educaci\xc3\xb3,_Joventut_i_Esports199658,_59,_60,_61,_62,_63,_64,_65_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMinisteri_d&#39;Educaci\xc3\xb3,_Joventut_i_Esports199658,_59,_60,_61,_62,_63,_64,_65-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009194,_195_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009194,_195-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009194,_195_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009194,_195-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009348_a_350_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009348_a_350-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESegal\xc3\xa0s201295_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESegal\xc3\xa0s201295-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The Council was replaced and new elections were held. But the economic situation worsened, as society was divided over the <i>Q\xc3\xbcesti\xc3\xb3 d\'Andorra</i> (the <i>Andorran Question</i> in relation to the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Question" title="Eastern Question">Eastern Question</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeruga_Guerrero199864,_65,_66,_67,_68_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeruga_Guerrero199864,_65,_66,_67,_68-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The struggles continued between pro-bishops, pro-French and nationalists who derived the troubles of Canillo in 1882 and 1885.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMinisteri_d&#39;Educaci\xc3\xb3,_Joventut_i_Esports199667_a_70_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMinisteri_d&#39;Educaci\xc3\xb3,_Joventut_i_Esports199667_a_70-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009198,_199,_202,_203_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009198,_199,_202,_203-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009352,_353_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009352,_353-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Andorra participated in the cultural movement of the Catalan <a href="/wiki/Renaixen%C3%A7a" title="Renaixen\xc3\xa7a">Renaixen\xc3\xa7a</a>. Between 1882 and 1887 the first academic schools were formed where trilingualism coexists with the knowledge of the official language, Catalan. Some <a href="/wiki/Romanticism" title="Romanticism">romantic</a> authors from both France and Spain reported the awakening of the <a href="/wiki/Romantic_nationalism" title="Romantic nationalism">national consciousness</a> of the country. <a href="/wiki/Jacint_Verdaguer" title="Jacint Verdaguer">Jacint Verdaguer</a> lived in Ordino during the 1880s where he wrote and share works related to the Renaixen\xc3\xa7a with <a href="/wiki/Casa_Rossell" title="Casa Rossell">Joaquim de Riba</a>, writer and photographer. <a href="/wiki/Fromental_Hal%C3%A9vy" title="Fromental Hal\xc3\xa9vy">Fromental Hal\xc3\xa9vy</a>, for his part, had already premiered in 1848 the opera <i><a href="/wiki/Le_val_d%27Andorre" title="Le val d&#39;Andorre">Le Val d\'Andorre</a></i> of great success in Europe, where the national consciousness of the valleys during the <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">Peninsular War</a> was exposed in the romantic work.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeruga_Guerrero199878,_79,_80,_81_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeruga_Guerrero199878,_79,_80,_81-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMinisteri_d&#39;Educaci\xc3\xb3,_Joventut_i_Esports199674_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMinisteri_d&#39;Educaci\xc3\xb3,_Joventut_i_Esports199674-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009354,_355,_356,_357_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009354,_355,_356,_357-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE\xc3\x80rea_de_Recerca_Hist\xc3\xb2rica_del_Govern_d&#39;Andorra200633_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE\xc3\x80rea_de_Recerca_Hist\xc3\xb2rica_del_Govern_d&#39;Andorra200633-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESegal\xc3\xa0s2012_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESegal\xc3\xa0s2012-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century:_Modernization_of_the_country_and_the_Constitutional_Andorra">20th century: Modernization of the country and the Constitutional Andorra</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 20th century: Modernization of the country and the Constitutional Andorra">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bor%C3%ADs_Sk%C3%B3syrev.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Bor%C3%ADs_Sk%C3%B3syrev.jpg/180px-Bor%C3%ADs_Sk%C3%B3syrev.jpg" width="180" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Bor%C3%ADs_Sk%C3%B3syrev.jpg/270px-Bor%C3%ADs_Sk%C3%B3syrev.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Bor%C3%ADs_Sk%C3%B3syrev.jpg/360px-Bor%C3%ADs_Sk%C3%B3syrev.jpg 2x" data-file-width="458" data-file-height="544" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bor%C3%ADs_Sk%C3%B3syrev.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Boris_Skossyreff" title="Boris Skossyreff">Boris Skossyreff</a>, briefly self-proclaimed "King of Andorra" in 1934.</div></div></div>\n<p>Andorra declared war on <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Germany">Imperial Germany</a> during World War I, but did not take part directly in the fighting. It is known that some Andorrans volunteered to take part in the conflict as part of the <a href="/wiki/Marching_Regiment_of_the_Foreign_Legion" title="Marching Regiment of the Foreign Legion">French Legions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> It remained in an official state of <a href="/wiki/Belligerency" class="mw-redirect" title="Belligerency">belligerency</a> until 1958 as it was not included in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DYKAndorra_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DYKAndorra-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1933, France occupied Andorra following social unrest which occurred before elections due the <i>Revolution of 1933</i> and the <i>FHASA strikes</i> (<i>Vagues de FHASA</i>); the revolt led by <i>Joves Andorrans</i> (a <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">labour union group</a> related to the Spanish <a href="/wiki/Confederaci%C3%B3n_Nacional_del_Trabajo" title="Confederaci\xc3\xb3n Nacional del Trabajo">CNT</a> and <a href="/wiki/Federaci%C3%B3n_Anarquista_Ib%C3%A9rica" title="Federaci\xc3\xb3n Anarquista Ib\xc3\xa9rica">FAI</a>) called for political reforms,<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage vote</a> of all Andorrans and acted in defense of the rights of local and foreign workers during the construction of FHASA\'s hydroelectric power station in <a href="/wiki/Encamp" title="Encamp">Encamp</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> The 5th April 1933 <i>Joves Andorrans</i> took the Andorran Parlamient under their custody in rebellion to their requests.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> These actions were preceded by the arrival of Colonel Ren\xc3\xa9-Jules Baulard with 50 <a href="/wiki/National_Gendarmerie" title="National Gendarmerie">gendarmes</a> and the mobilization of 200 local militias or <i>sometent</i> led by the S\xc3\xadndic Francesc Cairat.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 12 July 1934, adventurer <a href="/wiki/Boris_Skossyreff" title="Boris Skossyreff">Boris Skossyreff</a> issued a proclamation in Urgell, declaring himself "Boris I, King of Andorra", simultaneously declaring war on the Bishop of Urgell. He was arrested by the Spanish authorities on 20 July and ultimately expelled from <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>. From 1936 until 1940, a French military detachment was garrisoned in Andorra to secure the principality against disruption from the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francoist_Spain" title="Francoist Spain">Francoist Spain</a>. Francoist troops reached the Andorran border in the later stages of the war. During World War II, Andorra remained neutral and was an important smuggling route between <a href="/wiki/Vichy_France" title="Vichy France">Vichy France</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>.\n</p><p>Given its relative isolation, Andorra has existed outside the mainstream of European history, with few ties to countries other than <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>. In recent times, however, its thriving tourist industry along with developments in transport and communications have removed the country from its isolation. Since 1976 the country sees the need to reform Andorran institutions due to the anachronisms in the field of sovereignty, human rights and the balance of powers as well as the need to adapt legislation to modern demands. In 1982 a first separation of powers took place when instituting the <i>Govern d\'Andorra</i>, under the name of <i>Executive Board</i> (<i>Consell Executiu</i>), chaired by the first prime minister <a href="/wiki/%C3%92scar_Ribas_Reig" title="\xc3\x92scar Ribas Reig">\xc3\x92scar Ribas Reig</a> with the approval of the Co-Princes.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> In 1989 the Principality signed an agreement with the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> to regularize trade relations.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Its political system was modernized in 1993 after the <a href="/wiki/Andorran_constitutional_referendum,_1993" title="Andorran constitutional referendum, 1993">Andorran constitutional referendum</a>, when the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Andorra" title="Constitution of Andorra">constitution</a> was drafted by the Co-Princes and the General Council and approved on 14 March<sup id="cite_ref-NS_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NS-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> by 74.2% of voters, with a 76% turnout.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Andorran_parliamentary_election,_1993" title="Andorran parliamentary election, 1993">first elections</a> under the new constitution were held later in the year.<sup id="cite_ref-NS_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NS-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The same year Andorra became a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Andorra" title="Politics of Andorra">Politics of Andorra</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Co-princes_of_Andorra" class="mw-redirect" title="Co-princes of Andorra">Co-princes of Andorra</a></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:290px;max-width:290px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Mons._Vives_(30612833490).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Mons._Vives_%2830612833490%29.jpg/150px-Mons._Vives_%2830612833490%29.jpg" width="150" height="189" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Mons._Vives_%2830612833490%29.jpg/225px-Mons._Vives_%2830612833490%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Mons._Vives_%2830612833490%29.jpg/300px-Mons._Vives_%2830612833490%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="755" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><b><a href="/wiki/Joan_Enric_Vives_i_Sic%C3%ADlia" class="mw-redirect" title="Joan Enric Vives i Sic\xc3\xadlia">Joan Enric Vives i Sic\xc3\xadlia</a></b><br />&#160;&#8211;&#32; current <a href="/wiki/List_of_Co-Princes_of_Andorra" title="List of Co-Princes of Andorra">Catalan episcopal Co-Prince of Andorra</a> since 12 May 2003</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:134px;max-width:134px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Emmanuel_Macron_in_Tallinn_Digital_Summit._Welcome_dinner_hosted_by_HE_Donald_Tusk._Handshake_(36669381364)_(cropped_2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Emmanuel_Macron_in_Tallinn_Digital_Summit._Welcome_dinner_hosted_by_HE_Donald_Tusk._Handshake_%2836669381364%29_%28cropped_2%29.jpg/132px-Emmanuel_Macron_in_Tallinn_Digital_Summit._Welcome_dinner_hosted_by_HE_Donald_Tusk._Handshake_%2836669381364%29_%28cropped_2%29.jpg" width="132" height="190" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Emmanuel_Macron_in_Tallinn_Digital_Summit._Welcome_dinner_hosted_by_HE_Donald_Tusk._Handshake_%2836669381364%29_%28cropped_2%29.jpg/198px-Emmanuel_Macron_in_Tallinn_Digital_Summit._Welcome_dinner_hosted_by_HE_Donald_Tusk._Handshake_%2836669381364%29_%28cropped_2%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Emmanuel_Macron_in_Tallinn_Digital_Summit._Welcome_dinner_hosted_by_HE_Donald_Tusk._Handshake_%2836669381364%29_%28cropped_2%29.jpg/264px-Emmanuel_Macron_in_Tallinn_Digital_Summit._Welcome_dinner_hosted_by_HE_Donald_Tusk._Handshake_%2836669381364%29_%28cropped_2%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="437" data-file-height="630" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><b><a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Macron" title="Emmanuel Macron">Emmanuel Macron</a></b><br />&#160;&#8211;&#32; current <a href="/wiki/List_of_Co-Princes_of_Andorra" title="List of Co-Princes of Andorra">French Co-Prince of Andorra</a> since 14 May 2017</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>Andorra is a parliamentary <a href="/wiki/Co-principality" class="mw-redirect" title="Co-principality">co-principality</a> with the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_French_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="President of the French Republic">President of France</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a> <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Urgell" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop of Urgell">Bishop of Urgell</a> (<a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>) as <a href="/wiki/List_of_Co-Princes_of_Andorra" title="List of Co-Princes of Andorra">Co-Princes</a>. This peculiarity makes the President of France, in his capacity as <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Andorra" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince of Andorra">Prince of Andorra</a>, an elected reigning monarch, although he is not elected by a popular vote of the Andorran people. The politics of Andorra take place in a framework of a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a>, whereby the <a href="/wiki/List_of_heads_of_government_of_Andorra" title="List of heads of government of Andorra">Head of Government</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">chief executive</a>, and of a <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/pluriform" class="extiw" title="wiktionary:pluriform">pluriform</a> multi-party system.\n</p><p>The current Head of Government is <a href="/wiki/Antoni_Mart%C3%AD" title="Antoni Mart\xc3\xad">Antoni Mart\xc3\xad</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Democrats_for_Andorra" title="Democrats for Andorra">Democrats for Andorra</a> (DA). <a href="/wiki/Executive_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive power">Executive power</a> is exercised by the government. Legislative power is vested in both government and parliament.\n</p><p>The Parliament of Andorra is known as the General Council. The General Council consists of between 28 and 42 Councillors. The Councillors serve for four-year terms, and elections are held between the 30th and 40th days following the dissolution of the previous Council.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Casa_de_la_Vall_-_18.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Casa_de_la_Vall_-_18.jpg/220px-Casa_de_la_Vall_-_18.jpg" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Casa_de_la_Vall_-_18.jpg/330px-Casa_de_la_Vall_-_18.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Casa_de_la_Vall_-_18.jpg/440px-Casa_de_la_Vall_-_18.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3560" data-file-height="2222" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Casa_de_la_Vall_-_18.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Casa de la Vall, Historical and Ceremonial Andorran Parliament.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Casa_de_la_Vall,_Andorra_la_Vieja,_Andorra,_2013-12-30,_DD_03.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Andorra_la_Vieja%2C_Andorra%2C_2013-12-30%2C_DD_03.JPG/220px-Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Andorra_la_Vieja%2C_Andorra%2C_2013-12-30%2C_DD_03.JPG" width="220" height="78" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Andorra_la_Vieja%2C_Andorra%2C_2013-12-30%2C_DD_03.JPG/330px-Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Andorra_la_Vieja%2C_Andorra%2C_2013-12-30%2C_DD_03.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Andorra_la_Vieja%2C_Andorra%2C_2013-12-30%2C_DD_03.JPG/440px-Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Andorra_la_Vieja%2C_Andorra%2C_2013-12-30%2C_DD_03.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5426" data-file-height="1933" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Casa_de_la_Vall,_Andorra_la_Vieja,_Andorra,_2013-12-30,_DD_03.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/New_Parliament_of_Andorra" title="New Parliament of Andorra">New Parliament of Andorra</a>, <a href="/wiki/General_Council_of_Andorra" class="mw-redirect" title="General Council of Andorra">General Council</a> headquarter since 2011, next to <a href="/wiki/Casa_de_la_Vall" title="Casa de la Vall">Casa de la Vall</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Els_7_poetes,_Casa_de_la_Vall,_Consell_General.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Els_7_poetes%2C_Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Consell_General.JPG/220px-Els_7_poetes%2C_Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Consell_General.JPG" width="220" height="165"
