class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Els_7_poetes%2C_Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Consell_General.JPG/330px-Els_7_poetes%2C_Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Consell_General.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Els_7_poetes%2C_Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Consell_General.JPG/440px-Els_7_poetes%2C_Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Consell_General.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Els_7_poetes,_Casa_de_la_Vall,_Consell_General.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The centre of government in <a href="/wiki/Andorra_la_Vella" title="Andorra la Vella">Andorra la Vella</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Half are elected in equal numbers by each of the seven administrative parishes, and the other half of the Councillors are elected in a single national constituency. Fifteen days after the election, the Councillors hold their inauguration. During this session, the Syndic General, who is the head of the General Council, and the Subsyndic General, his assistant, are elected. Eight days later, the Council convenes once more. During this session the Head of Government is chosen from among the Councillors.\n</p><p>Candidates can be proposed by a minimum of one-fifth of the Councillors. The Council then elects the candidate with the absolute majority of votes to be Head of Government. The Syndic General then notifies the Co-Princes, who in turn appoint the elected candidate as the Head of Government of Andorra. The General Council is also responsible for proposing and passing laws. Bills may be presented to the Council as Private Members\' Bills by three of the local Parish Councils jointly or by at least one tenth of the citizens of Andorra.\n</p><p>The Council also approves the annual budget of the principality. The government must submit the proposed budget for parliamentary approval at least two months before the previous budget expires. If the budget is not approved by the first day of the next year, the previous budget is extended until a new one is approved. Once any bill is approved, the Syndic General is responsible for presenting it to the Co-Princes so that they may sign and enact it.\n</p><p>If the Head of Government is not satisfied with the Council, he may request that the Co-Princes dissolve the Council and order new elections. In turn, the Councillors have the power to remove the Head of Government from office. After a motion of censure is approved by at least one-fifth of the Councillors, the Council will vote and if it receives the absolute majority of votes, the Head of Government is removed.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_criminal_justice">Law and criminal justice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Law and criminal justice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Andorra" title="Law of Andorra">Law of Andorra</a></div>\n<p>The judiciary is composed of the Magistrates Court, the Criminal Law Court, the High Court of Andorra, and the Constitutional Court. The High Court of Justice is composed of five judges: one appointed by the Head of Government, one each by the Co-Princes, one by the Syndic General, and one by the Judges and Magistrates. It is presided over by the member appointed by the Syndic General and the judges hold office for six-year terms.\n</p><p>The Magistrates and Judges are appointed by the High Court, as is the President of the Criminal Law Court. The High Court also appoints members of the Office of the Attorney General. The Constitutional Court is responsible for interpreting the Constitution and reviewing all appeals of unconstitutionality against laws and treaties. It is composed of four judges, one appointed by each of the Co-Princes and two by the General Council. They serve eight-year terms. The Court is presided over by one of the Judges on a two-year rotation so that each judge at one point will preside over the Court.\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Foreign_relations.2C_defence.2C_and_security"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations,_defence,_and_security">Foreign relations, defence, and security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Foreign relations, defence, and security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Andorra" title="Foreign relations of Andorra">Foreign relations of Andorra</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bruxelles_rue_de_la_Montagne_10.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Bruxelles_rue_de_la_Montagne_10.jpg/220px-Bruxelles_rue_de_la_Montagne_10.jpg" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Bruxelles_rue_de_la_Montagne_10.jpg/330px-Bruxelles_rue_de_la_Montagne_10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Bruxelles_rue_de_la_Montagne_10.jpg/440px-Bruxelles_rue_de_la_Montagne_10.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3888" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bruxelles_rue_de_la_Montagne_10.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The embassy of Andorra in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Andorra does not have its own armed forces,<sup id="cite_ref-cia_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> although there is a small ceremonial army. Responsibility for defending the nation rests primarily with <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> However, in case of emergencies or natural disasters, the <i>Sometent</i> (an alarm) is called and all able-bodied men between 21 and 60 of Andorran nationality must serve.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-recarrega.net_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recarrega.net-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> This is why all Andorrans, and especially the head of each house (usually the eldest able-bodied man of a house) should, by law, keep a rifle, even though the law also states that the police will offer a firearm in case of need.<sup id="cite_ref-recarrega.net_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recarrega.net-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Andorra is a full member of the United Nations (UN), the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> (OSCE), and has a special agreement with the European Union (EU).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Andorra has a small army, which has historically been raised or reconstituted at various dates, but has never in modern times amounted to a standing army. The basic principle of Andorran defence is that all able-bodied men are available to fight if called upon by the sounding of the <i>Sometent</i>. Being a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a>, Andorra has no <a href="/wiki/Navy" title="Navy">navy</a>.\n</p><p>Prior to World War I, Andorra maintained an armed force of about 600 part-time militiamen. This body was not liable for service outside the principality and was commanded by two officials (<i>viguiers</i>) appointed by France and the Bishop of Urgell.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Despite not being involved in any fighting during the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a>, Andorra was technically the longest combatant, as the country was left out of the <a href="/wiki/Versailles_Peace_Conference" class="mw-redirect" title="Versailles Peace Conference">Versailles Peace Conference</a>, <a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">technically</a> remaining at war with Germany from its original declaration of war in 1914 until 24 September 1958 when Andorra officially declared peace with Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-DYKAndorra_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DYKAndorra-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the modern era, the army has consisted of a very small body of volunteers willing to undertake ceremonial duties. Uniforms were handed down from generation to generation within families and communities.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The army\'s role in internal security was largely taken over by the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Police_Corps_of_Andorra" title="Police Corps of Andorra">Police Corps of Andorra</a> in 1931. Brief civil disorder associated with the elections of 1933 led to assistance being sought from the French <a href="/wiki/National_Gendarmerie" title="National Gendarmerie">National Gendarmerie</a>, with a detachment resident in Andorra for two months under the command of Ren\xc3\xa9-Jules Baulard.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> The Andorran Army was reformed in the following year, with eleven soldiers appointed to supervisory roles.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The force consisted of six <a href="/wiki/Corporal" title="Corporal">Corporals</a>, one for each parish (although there are currently seven parishes, there were only six until 1978), plus four junior staff officers to co-ordinate action, and a commander with the rank of major. It was the responsibility of the six corporals, each in his own parish, to be able to raise a fighting force from among the able-bodied men of the parish.\n</p><p>Today a small, twelve-man ceremonial unit remains the only permanent section of the Andorran Army, but all able-bodied men remain technically available for military service,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> with a requirement for each family to have access to a firearm. The army has not fought for more than 700 years, and its main responsibility is to present the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Andorra" title="Flag of Andorra">flag of Andorra</a> at official ceremonial functions.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Marc_Forn%C3%A9_Moln%C3%A9" title="Marc Forn\xc3\xa9 Moln\xc3\xa9">Marc Forn\xc3\xa9 Moln\xc3\xa9</a>, Andorra\'s military budget is strictly from voluntary donations, and the availability of full-time volunteers.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The myth that all members of the Andorran Army are ranked as officers is popularly maintained in many works of reference.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> In reality, all those serving in the permanent ceremonial reserve hold ranks as <a href="/wiki/Officer_(armed_forces)" title="Officer (armed forces)">officers</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Non-commissioned_officer" title="Non-commissioned officer">non-commissioned officers</a>, because the <a href="/wiki/Enlisted_rank" title="Enlisted rank">other ranks</a> are considered to be the rest of the able-bodied male population, who may still be called upon by the <i>Sometent</i> to serve, although such a call has not been made in modern times.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Police_Corps">Police Corps</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Police Corps">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Police_Corps_of_Andorra" title="Police Corps of Andorra">Police Corps of Andorra</a></div>\n<p>Andorra maintains a small but modern and well-equipped internal police force, with around 240 police officers supported by civilian assistants. The principal services supplied by the corps are uniformed community policing, criminal detection, border control, and traffic policing. There are also small specialist units including police dogs, mountain rescue, and a bomb disposal team.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="GIPA">GIPA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: GIPA">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <i>Grup d\'Intervenci\xc3\xb3 Policia d\'Andorra</i> (GIPA) is a small special forces unit trained in <a href="/wiki/Counter-terrorism" title="Counter-terrorism">counter-terrorism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hostage_negotiator" class="mw-redirect" title="Hostage negotiator">hostage recovery</a> tasks. Although it is the closest in style to an active military force, it is part of the <a href="/wiki/Police_Corps_of_Andorra" title="Police Corps of Andorra">Police Corps</a>, and not the <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Andorra" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Andorra">army</a>. As terrorist and hostage situations are a rare threat to the country, the GIPA is commonly assigned to prisoner escort duties, and at other times to routine policing.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fire_brigade">Fire brigade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Fire brigade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <i>Andorran Fire Brigade</i>, with headquarters at <a href="/wiki/Santa_Coloma_d%27Andorra" title="Santa Coloma d&#39;Andorra">Santa Coloma</a>, operates from four modern fire stations, and has a staff of around 120 firefighters. The service is equipped with 16 heavy appliances (fire tenders, turntable ladders, and specialist four-wheel drive vehicles), four light support vehicles (cars and vans) and four ambulances.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Historically, the families of the six ancient parishes of Andorra maintained local arrangements to assist each other in fighting fires. The first fire pump purchased by the government was acquired in 1943. Serious fires which lasted for two days in December 1959 led to calls for a permanent fire service, and the <i>Andorran Fire Brigade</i> was formed on 21 April 1961.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The fire service maintains full-time cover with five fire crews on duty at any time: two at the brigade\'s headquarters in Santa Coloma, and one crew at each of the other three fire stations.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Andorramap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Andorramap.png/220px-Andorramap.png" width="220" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Andorramap.png/330px-Andorramap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Andorramap.png/440px-Andorramap.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="650" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Andorramap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Andorra with its seven parishes labelled.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Andorra_topographic_map-en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Andorra_topographic_map-en.svg/220px-Andorra_topographic_map-en.svg.png" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Andorra_topographic_map-en.svg/330px-Andorra_topographic_map-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Andorra_topographic_map-en.svg/440px-Andorra_topographic_map-en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1625" data-file-height="1300" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Andorra_topographic_map-en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Topographic map of Andorra.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Andorra" title="Geography of Andorra">Geography of Andorra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Andorra" title="Geology of Andorra">Geology of Andorra</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parishes">Parishes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Parishes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Parishes_of_Andorra" title="Parishes of Andorra">Parishes of Andorra</a></div>\n<p>Andorra consists of seven parishes:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Andorra_la_Vella" title="Andorra la Vella">Andorra la Vella</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Canillo" title="Canillo">Canillo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Encamp" title="Encamp">Encamp</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Escaldes-Engordany" title="Escaldes-Engordany">Escaldes-Engordany</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/La_Massana" title="La Massana">La Massana</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ordino" title="Ordino">Ordino</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sant_Juli%C3%A0_de_L%C3%B2ria" title="Sant Juli\xc3\xa0 de L\xc3\xb2ria">Sant Juli\xc3\xa0 de L\xc3\xb2ria</a></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_geography">Physical geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Physical geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Due to its location in the eastern <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a> mountain range, Andorra consists predominantly of rugged mountains, the highest being the <a href="/wiki/Coma_Pedrosa" title="Coma Pedrosa">Coma Pedrosa</a> at 2,942 metres (9,652&#160;ft), and the average elevation of Andorra is 1,996 metres (6,549&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> These are dissected by three narrow valleys in a Y shape that combine into one as the main stream, the <a href="/wiki/Gran_Valira" title="Gran Valira">Gran Valira</a> river, leaves the country for <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> (at Andorra\'s lowest point of 840&#160;m or 2,756&#160;ft). Andorra\'s land area is 468&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (181&#160;sq&#160;mi).\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Phytogeography" title="Phytogeography">Phytogeographically</a>, Andorra belongs to the Atlantic European province of the <a href="/wiki/Circumboreal_Region" title="Circumboreal Region">Circumboreal Region</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Boreal_Kingdom" title="Boreal Kingdom">Boreal Kingdom</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">WWF</a>, the territory of Andorra belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a> of Pyrenees conifer and mixed forests.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Andorra has an <a href="/wiki/Alpine_climate" title="Alpine climate">alpine climate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental climate</a>. Its higher elevation means there is, on average, more snow in winter, lower humidity, and it is slightly cooler in summer.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Andorra" title="Economy of Andorra">Economy of Andorra</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Andorra.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Tree_map_export_2009_Andorra.jpeg/220px-Tree_map_export_2009_Andorra.jpeg" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Tree_map_export_2009_Andorra.jpeg/330px-Tree_map_export_2009_Andorra.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Tree_map_export_2009_Andorra.jpeg/440px-Tree_map_export_2009_Andorra.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="501" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Andorra.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Exports in 2009</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Grandvalira_ski_resort,_Andorra5.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Grandvalira_ski_resort%2C_Andorra5.jpg/220px-Grandvalira_ski_resort%2C_Andorra5.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Grandvalira_ski_resort%2C_Andorra5.jpg/330px-Grandvalira_ski_resort%2C_Andorra5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Grandvalira_ski_resort%2C_Andorra5.jpg/440px-Grandvalira_ski_resort%2C_Andorra5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Grandvalira_ski_resort,_Andorra5.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Scenery of Andorran mountains in <i>Grand Valira</i> ski resort, <a href="/wiki/Soldeu" title="Soldeu">Soldeu</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Caldea_des_de_dins.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Caldea_des_de_dins.JPG/220px-Caldea_des_de_dins.JPG" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Caldea_des_de_dins.JPG/330px-Caldea_des_de_dins.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Caldea_des_de_dins.JPG/440px-Caldea_des_de_dins.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Caldea_des_de_dins.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Caldea" title="Caldea">Caldea</a> thermal spa, <a href="/wiki/Escaldes-Engordany" title="Escaldes-Engordany">Escaldes-Engordany</a>, the biggest thermoludic center in Southern Europe.</div></div></div>\n<p>Tourism, the mainstay of Andorra\'s tiny, well-to-do economy, accounts for roughly 80% of GDP. An estimated 10.2&#160;million tourists visit annually,<sup id="cite_ref-es2_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-es2-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> attracted by Andorra\'s duty-free status and by its summer and winter resorts.\n</p><p>One of the main sources of income in Andorra is tourism from ski resorts which total over 175&#160;km (109&#160;mi) of ski ground. The sport brings in over 10 million visitors annually and an estimated 340 million euros per year, sustaining 2,000 direct and 10,000 indirect jobs at present since 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The banking sector, with its <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax haven</a> status, also contributes substantially to the economy (the financial and insurance sector accounts for approximately 19% of GDP<sup id="cite_ref-fs2013_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fs2013-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>). The financial system comprises five banking groups,<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> one specialised credit entity, 8 investment undertaking management entities, 3 asset management companies and 29 insurance companies, 14 of which are branches of foreign insurance companies authorised to operate in the principality.<sup id="cite_ref-fs2013_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fs2013-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Agricultural production is limited, only 2% of the land is arable, and most food has to be imported. Some tobacco is grown locally. The principal livestock activity is domestic sheep raising. Manufacturing output consists mainly of cigarettes, cigars, and furniture. Andorra\'s natural resources include hydroelectric power, mineral water, timber, iron ore, and lead.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Andorra is not a member of the European Union, but enjoys a <a href="/wiki/Andorra%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Andorra\xe2\x80\x93European Union relations">special relationship</a> with it, such as being treated as an EU member for trade in manufactured goods (no tariffs) and as a non-EU member for agricultural products. Andorra lacked a currency of its own and used both the <a href="/wiki/French_franc" title="French franc">French franc</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_peseta" title="Spanish peseta">Spanish peseta</a> in banking transactions until 31 December 1999, when both currencies were replaced by the EU\'s single currency, the euro. Coins and notes of both the franc and the peseta remained legal tender in Andorra until 31 December 2002. Andorra negotiated to issue its own euro coins, beginning in 2014.\n</p><p>Andorra has traditionally had one of the world\'s lowest unemployment rates. In 2009 it stood at 2.9%.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Andorra has long benefited from its status as a tax haven, with revenues raised exclusively through import tariffs. However, during the <a href="/wiki/European_sovereign-debt_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="European sovereign-debt crisis">European sovereign-debt crisis</a> of the 21st century, its tourist economy suffered a decline, partly caused by a drop in the prices of goods in <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, which undercut Andorran <a href="/wiki/Duty-free_shop" title="Duty-free shop">duty-free shopping</a>. This led to a growth in unemployment. On 1 January 2012, a business tax of 10% was introduced,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> followed by a <a href="/wiki/Sales_tax" title="Sales tax">sales tax</a> of 2% a year later, which raised just over 14 million euros in its first quarter.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 31 May 2013, it was announced that Andorra intended to legislate for the introduction of an <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a> by the end of June, against a background of increasing dissatisfaction with the existence of tax havens among EU members.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> The announcement was made following a meeting in Paris between the Head of Government <a href="/wiki/Antoni_Marti" class="mw-redirect" title="Antoni Marti">Antoni Marti</a> and the French President and Prince of Andorra, <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Hollande" title="Fran\xc3\xa7ois Hollande">Fran\xc3\xa7ois Hollande</a>. Hollande welcomed the move as part of a process of Andorra "bringing its taxation in line with international standards".<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Andorra_Vall_dels_Cortals_05_JMM.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Andorra_Vall_dels_Cortals_05_JMM.JPG/220px-Andorra_Vall_dels_Cortals_05_JMM.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Andorra_Vall_dels_Cortals_05_JMM.JPG/330px-Andorra_Vall_dels_Cortals_05_JMM.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Andorra_Vall_dels_Cortals_05_JMM.JPG/440px-Andorra_Vall_dels_Cortals_05_JMM.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Andorra_Vall_dels_Cortals_05_JMM.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The town of Encamp, Andorra, as seen from the Vall dels Cortals</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Andorra" title="Demographics of Andorra">Demographics of Andorra</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 0.5em;"><tbody><tr><th class="navbox-title" colspan="3" style="padding:0.25em;font-size:110%">Historical populations</th></tr><tr style="font-size:95%"><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;width:3em">Year</th><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px 2px;text-align:right"><abbr title="Population">Pop.</abbr></th><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;text-align:right"><abbr title="Per annum growth rate">\xc2\xb1% p.a.</abbr></th></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2000</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">65,844</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+1.91%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2010</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">85,015</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+2.59%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2015</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">78,014</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">\xe2\x88\x921.70%</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left">Source: Departament d\'Estad\xc3\xadstica d\'Andorra<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The population of Andorra is estimated at 77,281 (2016).<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Andorran_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Andorran people">Andorrans</a> are a <a href="/wiki/Italic_peoples" title="Italic peoples">Romance</a> <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic group</a> of originally <a href="/wiki/Catalans" title="Catalans">Catalan</a> descent.<sup id="cite_ref-Minahan_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minahan-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The population has grown from 5,000 in 1900.\n</p><p>Two-thirds of residents lack Andorran nationality and do not have the right to vote in communal elections. Moreover, they are not allowed to be elected as prime minister<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> or to own more than 33% of the capital stock of a privately held company.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Andorra" title="Languages of Andorra">Languages of Andorra</a></div>\n<p>The historic and <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> is <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Romance_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Romance language">Romance language</a>. The Andorran government encourages the use of Catalan. It funds a Commission for Catalan <a href="/wiki/Toponymy" title="Toponymy">Toponymy</a> in Andorra (Catalan: <i>la Comissi\xc3\xb3 de Topon\xc3\xadmia d\'Andorra</i>), and provides free Catalan classes to assist immigrants. Andorran television and radio stations use Catalan.\n</p><p>Because of immigration, historical links, and close geographic proximity, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> are also commonly spoken. Most Andorran residents can speak one or more of these, in addition to Catalan. English is less commonly spoken among the general population, though it is understood to varying degrees in the major tourist resorts. Andorra is one of only four European countries (together with France, Monaco, and Turkey)<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> that have never signed the <a href="/wiki/Framework_Convention_for_the_Protection_of_National_Minorities" title="Framework Convention for the Protection of National Minorities">Council of Europe Framework Convention on National Minorities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the <i>Observatori Social d\'Andorra</i>, the linguistic usage in Andorra is as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table border="0" style="border:1px solid #999; background:#fff;">\n\n<tbody><tr style="text-align:center;">\n<th style="background:#ccc;">Mother tongue</th>\n<th>%\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td style="background:#ccc;"><a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a></td>\n<td>38.8%\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td style="background:#ccc;">Spanish</td>\n<td>35.4%\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td style="background:#ccc;"><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a></td>\n<td>15%\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td style="background:#ccc;">French</td>\n<td>5.4%\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td style="background:#ccc;">Others</td>\n<td>5.5%\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td colspan="2"><small><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20130822055051/http://www.iea.ad/images/stories/Documents/CRES/Observatoris/2005/2005_3_PoliticaLinguistica.pdf">2005 3 PoliticaLinguistica.pdf</a></small>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The population of Andorra is predominantly (88.2%) Catholic.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Their patron saint is <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Meritxell" title="Our Lady of Meritxell">Our Lady of Meritxell</a>. Though it is not an official state religion, the constitution acknowledges a special relationship with the Catholic Church, offering some special privileges to that group<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (August 2014)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. Other Christian denominations include the <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican Church">Anglican Church</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Unification_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Unification Church">Unification Church</a>, the <a href="/wiki/New_Apostolic_Church" title="New Apostolic Church">New Apostolic Church</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Jehovah\'s Witnesses</a>. The small <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Andorra" title="Islam in Andorra">Muslim community</a> is primarily made up of North African immigrants.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> There is a small community of <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hindus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_in_Andorra" title="Bah\xc3\xa1&#39;\xc3\xad Faith in Andorra">Bah\xc3\xa1\'\xc3\xads</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ARDA05_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARDA05-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wolfram_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wolfram-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> and roughly 100 Jews live in Andorra.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> (See <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Andorra" title="History of the Jews in Andorra">History of the Jews in Andorra</a>.)\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics">Statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_cities">Largest cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Largest cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Andorra" class="mw-redirect" title="List of cities in Andorra">List of cities in Andorra</a></div>\n<table class="navbox">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="10" class="navbox-title"><div style="float:right; width:6em; style="text-align:right;">2,025\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">10</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Arinsal" title="Arinsal">Arinsal</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/La_Massana" title="La Massana">La Massana</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">1,555\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Schools">Schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Children between the ages of 6 and 16 are required by law to have full-time education. Education up to secondary level is provided free of charge by the government.\n</p><p>There are three systems of school, Andorran, French and Spanish, which use Catalan, French and Spanish languages respectively, as the main language of instruction. Parents may choose which system their children attend. All schools are built and maintained by Andorran authorities, but teachers in the French and Spanish schools are paid for the most part by <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>. 39% of Andorran children attend Andorran schools, 33% attend French schools, and 28% Spanish schools.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="University_of_Andorra">University of Andorra</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: University of Andorra">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Universitat_d%27Andorra" title="Universitat d&#39;Andorra">Universitat d\'Andorra</a> (UdA) is the state public university and is the only university in Andorra. It was established in 1997. The university provides first-level degrees in nursing, computer science, business administration, and educational sciences, in addition to higher professional education courses. The only two graduate schools in Andorra are the Nursing School and the School of Computer Science, the latter having a PhD programme.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Virtual_Studies_Centre">Virtual Studies Centre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Virtual Studies Centre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The geographical complexity of the country as well as the small number of students prevents the University of Andorra from developing a full academic programme, and it serves principally as a centre for virtual studies, connected to Spanish and French universities. The Virtual Studies Centre (<i>Centre d\'Estudis Virtuals</i>) at the University runs approximately twenty different academic degrees at both undergraduate and postgraduate levels in fields including tourism, law, Catalan philology, humanities, psychology, political sciences, audiovisual communication, telecommunications engineering, and East Asia studies. The Centre also runs various postgraduate programmes and continuing-education courses for professionals.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Healthcare in Andorra is provided to all employed persons and their families by the government-run social security system, <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caixa_Andorrana_de_Seguretat_Social&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Caixa Andorrana de Seguretat Social (page does not exist)">Caixa Andorrana de Seguretat Social</a></i> (CASS), which is funded by employer and employee contributions in respect of salaries. The cost of healthcare is covered by CASS at rates of 75% for out-patient expenses such as medicines and hospital visits, 90% for hospitalisation, and 100% for work-related accidents. The remainder of the costs may be covered by private health insurance. Other residents and tourists require full private health insurance.<sup id="cite_ref-travenand_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-travenand-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The main hospital, Meritxell, is in <a href="/wiki/Escaldes-Engordany" title="Escaldes-Engordany">Escaldes-Engordany</a>. There are also 12 primary health care centres in various locations around the principality.<sup id="cite_ref-cassps_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cassps-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Andorra" title="Transport in Andorra">Transport in Andorra</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Andorra%E2%80%93La_Seu_d%27Urgell_Airport" title="Andorra\xe2\x80\x93La Seu d&#39;Urgell Airport">Andorra\xe2\x80\x93La Seu d\'Urgell Airport</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AGC_Z_27500.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/AGC_Z_27500.jpg/220px-AGC_Z_27500.jpg" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/AGC_Z_27500.jpg/330px-AGC_Z_27500.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/AGC_Z_27500.jpg/440px-AGC_Z_27500.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AGC_Z_27500.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A train at <a href="/wiki/Latour-de-Carol" title="Latour-de-Carol">Latour-de-Carol</a> (<i>La Tor de Querol</i>), one of the two stations serving Andorra. Andorra has no railways, although the line connecting Latour-de-Carol and <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a>, which in turn connects to France\'s <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">TGVs</a> at Toulouse, runs within two kilometres (1.2 miles) of the Andorran border.</div></div></div>\n<p>Until the 20th century, Andorra had very limited transport links to the outside world, and development of the country was affected by its physical isolation. Even now, the nearest major airports at Toulouse and Barcelona are both three hours\' drive from Andorra.\n</p><p>Andorra has a road network of 279&#160;km (173&#160;mi), of which 76&#160;km (47&#160;mi) is unpaved. The two main roads out of <a href="/wiki/Andorra_la_Vella" title="Andorra la Vella">Andorra la Vella</a> are the CG-1 to the Spanish border, and the CG-2 to the French border via the Envalira Tunnel near <a href="/wiki/El_Pas_de_la_Casa" title="El Pas de la Casa">El Pas de la Casa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mobi_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mobi-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Bus services cover all metropolitan areas and many rural communities, with services on most major routes running half-hourly or more frequently during peak travel times. There are frequent long-distance bus services from Andorra to <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a>, plus a daily tour from the former city. Bus services are mostly run by private companies, but some local ones are operated by the government.\n</p><p>There are no airports for fixed-wing aircraft within Andorra\'s borders but there are, however, heliports in <a href="/wiki/La_Massana" title="La Massana">La Massana</a> (Cam\xc3\xad Heliport), <a href="/wiki/Arinsal" title="Arinsal">Arinsal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Escaldes-Engordany" title="Escaldes-Engordany">Escaldes-Engordany</a> with commercial helicopter services<sup id="cite_ref-heliand_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heliand-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-helitrans_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-helitrans-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> and an airport located in the neighbouring Spanish comarca of <a href="/wiki/Alt_Urgell" title="Alt Urgell">Alt Urgell</a>, 12 kilometres (7.5 miles) south of the Andorran-Spanish border.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Since July 2015, <a href="/wiki/Andorra%E2%80%93La_Seu_d%27Urgell_Airport" title="Andorra\xe2\x80\x93La Seu d&#39;Urgell Airport">Andorra\xe2\x80\x93La Seu d\'Urgell Airport</a> has operated commercial flights to <a href="/wiki/Adolfo_Su%C3%A1rez_Madrid%E2%80%93Barajas_Airport" title="Adolfo Su\xc3\xa1rez Madrid\xe2\x80\x93Barajas Airport">Madrid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palma_de_Mallorca_Airport" title="Palma de Mallorca Airport">Palma de Mallorca</a>, and is the <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">main hub</a> for <a href="/wiki/Air_Andorra" title="Air Andorra">Air Andorra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andorra_Airlines" title="Andorra Airlines">Andorra Airlines</a>.\n</p><p>Nearby airports located in <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> provide access to international flights for the principality. The nearest airports are at <a href="/wiki/Perpignan%E2%80%93Rivesaltes_Airport" title="Perpignan\xe2\x80\x93Rivesaltes Airport">Perpignan</a>, France (156 kilometres or 97 miles from Andorra) and <a href="/wiki/Lleida-Alguaire_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Lleida-Alguaire Airport">Lleida</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> (160 kilometres or 99 miles from Andorra). The largest nearby airports are at <a href="/wiki/Toulouse%E2%80%93Blagnac_Airport" title="Toulouse\xe2\x80\x93Blagnac Airport">Toulouse</a>, France (165 kilometres or 103 miles from Andorra) and <a href="/wiki/Barcelona_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Barcelona Airport">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> (215 kilometres or 134 miles from Andorra). There are hourly bus services from both Barcelona and Toulouse airports to Andorra.\n</p><p>The nearest railway station is <a href="/wiki/L%27Hospitalet-pr%C3%A8s-l%27Andorre" title="L&#39;Hospitalet-pr\xc3\xa8s-l&#39;Andorre">L\'Hospitalet-pr\xc3\xa8s-l\'Andorre</a> 10&#160;km (6&#160;mi) east of Andorra which is on the <span class="nowrap">1,435&#160;mm</span> (<span class="nowrap">4&#160;ft&#160;<span class="frac">8<span class="visualhide">&#160;</span><sup>1</sup>&#8260;<sub>2</sub></span>&#160;in</span>)<a href="/wiki/Standard_gauge" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard gauge">-gauge</a> line from <a href="/wiki/Latour-de-Carol" title="Latour-de-Carol">Latour-de-Carol</a> (25&#160;km or 16&#160;mi) southeast of Andorra, to <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a> and on to Paris by the French <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">high-speed trains</a>. This line is operated by the <a href="/wiki/SNCF" title="SNCF">SNCF</a>. Latour-de-Carol has a scenic <span class="nowrap">1,000&#160;mm</span> (<span class="nowrap">3&#160;ft&#160;<span class="frac">3<span class="visualhide">&#160;</span><sup>3</sup>&#8260;<sub>8</sub></span>&#160;in</span>) <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Metre_gauge" class="mw-redirect" title="Metre gauge">metre gauge</a></span> <a href="/wiki/Yellow_Train" class="mw-redirect" title="Yellow Train">trainline</a> to <a href="/wiki/Villefranche-de-Conflent" title="Villefranche-de-Conflent">Villefranche-de-Conflent</a>, as well as the SNCF\'s <span class="nowrap">1,435&#160;mm</span> gauge line connecting to <a href="/wiki/Perpignan" title="Perpignan">Perpignan</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/RENFE" class="mw-redirect" title="RENFE">RENFE\'s</a> <span class="nowrap">1,668&#160;mm</span> (<span class="nowrap">5&#160;ft&#160;<span class="frac">5<span class="visualhide">&#160;</span><sup>21</sup>&#8260;<sub>32</sub></span>&#160;in</span>) <a href="/wiki/Iberian_gauge" class="mw-redirect" title="Iberian gauge">-gauge</a> line to <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> There are also direct <a href="/wiki/Intercit%C3%A9s#Night_trains" title="Intercit\xc3\xa9s">Intercit\xc3\xa9s de Nuit</a> trains between L\'Hospitalet-pr\xc3\xa8s-l\'Andorre and Paris on certain dates.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_telecommunications">Media and telecommunications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Media and telecommunications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Andorra" title="Telecommunications in Andorra">Telecommunications in Andorra</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Andorra_Telecom" title="Andorra Telecom">Andorra Telecom</a></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small><i>(November 2015)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In Andorra, mobile and fixed telephone and internet services are operated exclusively by the Andorran national telecommunications company, SOM, also known as <a href="/wiki/Andorra_Telecom" title="Andorra Telecom">Andorra Telecom</a> (STA). The same company also manages the technical infrastructure for national broadcasting of digital television and radio.\n</p><p>By the end of 2010, it was planned that every home in the country would have fibre-to-the-home for internet access at a minimum speed of 100&#160;Mbit/s,<sup id="cite_ref-somfo_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-somfo-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> and the availability was complete in June 2012.\n</p><p>There is only one Andorran television station, <i><a href="/wiki/R%C3%A0dio_i_Televisi%C3%B3_d%27Andorra" title="R\xc3\xa0dio i Televisi\xc3\xb3 d&#39;Andorra">R\xc3\xa0dio i Televisi\xc3\xb3 d\'Andorra</a></i> (RTVA). <i>Radio Nacional d\'Andorra</i> operates two radio stations, <i><a href="/wiki/Radio_Andorra" title="Radio Andorra">Radio Andorra</a></i> and <i>Andorra M\xc3\xbasica</i>. There are three national newspapers, <i><a href="/wiki/Diari_d%27Andorra" title="Diari d&#39;Andorra">Diari d\'Andorra</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/El_Peri%C3%B2dic_d%27Andorra" title="El Peri\xc3\xb2dic d&#39;Andorra">El Peri\xc3\xb2dic d\'Andorra</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Bondia_(newspaper)" title="Bondia (newspaper)">Bondia</a></i> as well as several local newspapers.  There is also an <a href="/wiki/Amateur_radio" title="Amateur radio">amateur radio</a> society.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Additional TV and radio stations from <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> are available via digital terrestrial television and IPTV.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Andorra" title="Culture of Andorra">Culture of Andorra</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Andorra" title="Music of Andorra">Music of Andorra</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HPIM0309.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/HPIM0309.JPG/220px-HPIM0309.JPG" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/HPIM0309.JPG/330px-HPIM0309.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/HPIM0309.JPG/440px-HPIM0309.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="2144" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HPIM0309.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Andorran flag on balcony, Ordino</div></div></div>\n<p>The official and historic language is Catalan. Thus the culture is Catalan, with its own specificity.\n</p><p>Andorra is home to folk dances like the contrap\xc3\xa0s and marratxa, which survive in <a href="/wiki/Sant_Juli%C3%A0_de_L%C3%B2ria" title="Sant Juli\xc3\xa0 de L\xc3\xb2ria">Sant Juli\xc3\xa0 de L\xc3\xb2ria</a> especially. Andorran folk music has similarities to the music of its neighbours, but is especially <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Catalonia" title="Music of Catalonia">Catalan</a> in character, especially in the presence of dances such as the <a href="/wiki/Sardana" title="Sardana">sardana</a>. Other Andorran folk dances include contrap\xc3\xa0s in <a href="/wiki/Andorra_la_Vella" title="Andorra la Vella">Andorra la Vella</a> and Saint Anne\'s dance in Escaldes-Engordany. Andorra\'s national holiday is <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Meritxell" title="Our Lady of Meritxell">Our Lady of Meritxell</a> Day, 8 September.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> American folk artist <a href="/wiki/Malvina_Reynolds" title="Malvina Reynolds">Malvina Reynolds</a>, intrigued by its defence budget of $4.90, wrote a song "Andorra". <a href="/wiki/Pete_Seeger" title="Pete Seeger">Pete Seeger</a> added verses, and sang "Andorra" on his 1962 album <i>The Bitter and the Sweet</i>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Andorra is famous for the practice of <a href="/wiki/Winter_sports" class="mw-redirect" title="Winter sports">winter sports</a>. Popular sports played in Andorra include <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roller_hockey_(quad)" title="Roller hockey (quad)">roller hockey</a>.\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Roller_hockey_(quad)" title="Roller hockey (quad)">roller hockey</a> Andorra usually plays in <a href="/wiki/CERH_European_Roller_Hockey_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="CERH European Roller Hockey Championship">CERH Euro Cup</a> and in <a href="/wiki/FIRS_Roller_Hockey_World_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="FIRS Roller Hockey World Cup">FIRS Roller Hockey World Cup</a>. In 2011, Andorra was the host country to the <a href="/wiki/2011_European_League_Final_Eight" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 European League Final Eight">2011 European League Final Eight</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Estadi_Comunal_Vella.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Estadi_Comunal_Vella.jpg/220px-Estadi_Comunal_Vella.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Estadi_Comunal_Vella.jpg/330px-Estadi_Comunal_Vella.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Estadi_Comunal_Vella.jpg/440px-Estadi_Comunal_Vella.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2832" data-file-height="2128" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Estadi_Comunal_Vella.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Estadi_Comunal_d%27Andorra_la_Vella" title="Estadi Comunal d&#39;Andorra la Vella">Estadi Comunal d\'Andorra la Vella</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The country is represented in association football by the <a href="/wiki/Andorra_national_football_team" title="Andorra national football team">Andorra national football team</a>. However, the team has had little success internationally because of Andorra\'s small population.<sup id="cite_ref-fifa_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fifa-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> Football is governed in Andorra by the <a href="/wiki/Andorran_Football_Federation" title="Andorran Football Federation">Andorran Football Federation</a> - founded in 1994, it organizes the national competitions of association football (<a href="/wiki/Primera_Divisi%C3%B3" title="Primera Divisi\xc3\xb3">Primera Divisi\xc3\xb3</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copa_Constituci%C3%B3" title="Copa Constituci\xc3\xb3">Copa Constituci\xc3\xb3</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andorran_Supercup" title="Andorran Supercup">Supercopa</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">futsal</a>. Andorra was admitted to <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> and <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> in the same year, 1996. <a href="/wiki/FC_Andorra" title="FC Andorra">FC Andorra</a>, a club based in <a href="/wiki/Andorra_la_Vella" title="Andorra la Vella">Andorra la Vella</a> founded in 1942, compete in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_football_league_system" title="Spanish football league system">Spanish football league system</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">Rugby</a> is a traditional sport in Andorra, mainly influenced by the popularity in southern France. The <a href="/wiki/Andorra_national_rugby_union_team" title="Andorra national rugby union team">Andorra national rugby union team</a>, nicknamed "<i>Els Isards</i>", has impressed on the international stage in <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_sevens" title="Rugby sevens">rugby sevens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/VPC_Andorra_XV" title="VPC Andorra XV">VPC Andorra XV</a> is a rugby team based in <a href="/wiki/Andorra_la_Vella" title="Andorra la Vella">Andorra la Vella</a> actually playing in the French championship.\n</p><p>Basketball popularity has increased in the country since the 1990s, when the Andorran team <a href="/wiki/BC_Andorra" title="BC Andorra">BC Andorra</a> played in the top league of <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> (<a href="/wiki/Liga_ACB" title="Liga ACB">Liga ACB</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> After 18 years the club returned to the top league in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other sports practised in Andorra include <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">cycling</a>, volleyball, <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">judo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australian_Rules_football" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian Rules football">Australian Rules football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Handball" title="Handball">handball</a>, swimming, gymnastics, tennis and <a href="/wiki/Motorsports" class="mw-redirect" title="Motorsports">motorsports</a>. In 2012, Andorra raised its first national <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a> team and played a home match against the Dutch Fellowship of Fairly Odd Places Cricket Club, the first match played in the history of Andorra at an altitude of 1,300 metres (4,300&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Andorra first participated at the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a> in 1976. The country has also appeared in every <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympic" class="mw-redirect" title="Winter Olympic">Winter Olympic</a> Games since <a href="/wiki/1976_Winter_Olympics" title="1976 Winter Olympics">1976</a>. Andorra competes in the <a href="/wiki/Games_of_the_Small_States_of_Europe" title="Games of the Small States of Europe">Games of the Small States of Europe</a> being twice the host country in <a href="/wiki/1991_Games_of_the_Small_States_of_Europe" title="1991 Games of the Small States of Europe">1991</a> and <a href="/wiki/2005_Games_of_the_Small_States_of_Europe" title="2005 Games of the Small States of Europe">2005</a>.\n</p><p>As part of the Catalan cultural ambit, Andorra is home to a team of <a href="/wiki/Castell" title="Castell">castellers</a>, or Catalan human tower builders. The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Castellers_d%27Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Castellers d&#39;Andorra (page does not exist)">Castellers d\'Andorra</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://ca.wikipedia.org/wiki/Castellers_d%27Andorra" class="extiw" title="ca:Castellers d&#39;Andorra">ca</a>)</span>, based in the town of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Coloma_d%27Andorra" title="Santa Coloma d&#39;Andorra">Santa Coloma d\'Andorra</a>, are recognized by the <a href="https://ca.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coordinadora_de_Colles_Castelleres_de_Catalunya" class="extiw" title="ca:Coordinadora de Colles Castelleres de Catalunya">Coordinadora de Colles Castelleres de Catalunya</a>, the governing body of castells.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_achievements">Major achievements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Major achievements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Ariadna_Tudel_Cuberes" title="Ariadna Tudel Cuberes">Ariadna Tudel Cuberes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sophie_Dusautoir_Bertrand" title="Sophie Dusautoir Bertrand">Sophie Dusautoir Bertrand</a> earned the bronze medal in the women\'s team competition at the <a href="/wiki/2009_European_Championship_of_Ski_Mountaineering" title="2009 European Championship of Ski Mountaineering">2009 European Championship of Ski Mountaineering</a>. <a href="/wiki/Joan_Verdu_Sanchez" title="Joan Verdu Sanchez">Joan Verdu Sanchez</a> earned a bronze medal in <a href="/wiki/Alpine_skiing_at_the_2012_Winter_Youth_Olympics" title="Alpine skiing at the 2012 Winter Youth Olympics">Alpine Skiing at the 2012 Winter Youth Olympics</a>. In 2015, <a href="/wiki/Marc_Oliveras" title="Marc Oliveras">Marc Oliveras</a> earned a silver medal in <a href="/wiki/Alpine_skiing_at_the_2015_Winter_Universiade" title="Alpine skiing at the 2015 Winter Universiade">Alpine Skiing at the 2015 Winter Universiade</a>, while <a href="/w/index.php?title=Carmina_Pallas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Carmina Pallas (page does not exist)">Carmina Pallas</a> earned a silver and a bronze medal in the same competition.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul portal</a></span></li></ul></div>\n<table role="presentation" class="metadata mbox-small" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td class="mbox-image"><img
